Scotland</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Nicola Ferguson Sturgeon</b> (born 19 July 1970) is a Scottish politician serving as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_First_Ministers_of_Scotland" title="List of First Ministers of Scotland">fifth</a> and current <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a> and leader of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP) since November 2014. She is the first woman to hold either position. Sturgeon has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> since 1999, first as an <a href="/wiki/Additional_member_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Additional member system">additional member</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Glasgow (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Glasgow electoral region</a> from 1999 to 2007 and as the member for <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Southside_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Southside (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Glasgow Southside</a> since 2007 (known as <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Govan_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Govan (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Glasgow Govan</a> from 2007 to 2011).\n</p><p>A law graduate of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, Sturgeon worked as a <a href="/wiki/Solicitor" title="Solicitor">solicitor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>. After being elected to the Scottish Parliament, she served successively as the SNP\'s shadow minister for education, health, and justice. In 2004 she announced that she would stand as a candidate for the leadership of the SNP following the resignation of <a href="/wiki/John_Swinney" title="John Swinney">John Swinney</a>. However, she later withdrew from the contest in favour of <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a>, standing instead as <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/depute" class="extiw" title="wikt:depute">depute</a> (deputy) leader on a joint ticket with Salmond.\n</p><p>Both were subsequently elected, and as Salmond was still an MP in the House of Commons, Sturgeon led the SNP in the Scottish Parliament from 2004 to 2007. The SNP won the highest number of seats in the Scottish Parliament in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_general_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament general election, 2007">the 2007 election</a> and Salmond was subsequently appointed First Minister. He appointed Sturgeon as <a href="/wiki/Deputy_First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="Deputy First Minister of Scotland">Deputy First Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Health_and_Wellbeing" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing">Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing</a>. She was appointed as <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Infrastructure,_Investment_and_Cities" title="Cabinet Secretary for Infrastructure, Investment and Cities">Cabinet Secretary for Infrastructure, Investment and Cities</a> in 2012.\n</p><p>Following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">"Yes"</a> campaign in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a>, Salmond announced that he would be resigning as party leader at the SNP party conference that November, and would resign as First Minister after a new leader was chosen.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> No one else was nominated for the post by the time nominations closed, leaving Sturgeon to <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party_leadership_election,_2014" title="Scottish National Party leadership election, 2014">take the party leadership unopposed</a> at the SNP\'s annual conference. She was formally elected to succeed Salmond as First Minister on 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine ranked Sturgeon as the 50th most powerful woman in the world in 2016 and 2nd in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_powerful_women_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_powerful_women-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Hour" title="Woman&#39;s Hour">Woman\'s Hour</a></i> assessed Sturgeon to be the most powerful and influential woman in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life_and_education"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life and education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Early_political_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Early political career</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Depute_Leader_and_Deputy_First_Minister"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Depute Leader and Deputy First Minister</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Leadership_of_the_Scottish_National_Party"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Leadership of the Scottish National Party</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#First_Minister_of_Scotland"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">First Minister of Scotland</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#First_term,_2014\xe2\x80\x932016"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">First term, 2014\xe2\x80\x932016</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7"><a href="#UK_2015_general_election"><span class="tocnumber">5.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">UK 2015 general election</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8"><a href="#Scottish_Parliament_election,_2016"><span class="tocnumber">5.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Scottish Parliament election, 2016</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Second_term,_2016\xe2\x80\x93"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Second term, 2016\xe2\x80\x93</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#2016_EU_membership_referendum"><span class="tocnumber">5.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">2016 EU membership referendum</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Future_referendum_on_independence"><span class="tocnumber">5.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Future referendum on independence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#European_Union_membership"><span class="tocnumber">5.2.3</span> <span class="toctext">European Union membership</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#Scottish_local_elections,_2017"><span class="tocnumber">5.2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Scottish local elections, 2017</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#International_relations"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">International relations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#Catalonian_independence_referendum,_2017"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Catalonian independence referendum, 2017</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#United_States"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">United States</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Spain"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Spain</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#Germany"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Germany</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Republic_of_Ireland"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Republic of Ireland</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Political_views"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Political views</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Awards_and_acknowledgements"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and acknowledgements</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span></h2>\n<p>Nicola Ferguson Sturgeon<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> was born in <a href="/wiki/Ayrshire_Central_Hospital" title="Ayrshire Central Hospital">Ayrshire Central Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_North_Ayrshire" title="Irvine, North Ayrshire">Irvine</a>, on 19 July 1970. She is the eldest of three daughters born to Robin Sturgeon (born 1948), an electrician, and Joan Kerr Sturgeon (<i>n\xc3\xa9e</i> Ferguson, born 1952), a <a href="/wiki/Registered_Dental_Nurse" title="Registered Dental Nurse">dental nurse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Her family has some roots in <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East England</a>; her paternal grandmother was from <a href="/wiki/Ryhope" title="Ryhope">Ryhope</a> in what is now the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">City of Sunderland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon grew up in <a href="/wiki/Prestwick" title="Prestwick">Prestwick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dreghorn" title="Dreghorn">Dreghorn</a>. She attended Dreghorn Primary School from 1975 to 1982 and <a href="/wiki/Greenwood_Academy,_Dreghorn" title="Greenwood Academy, Dreghorn">Greenwood Academy</a> from 1982 to 1988. She later studied at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, where she read <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">Law</a>. Sturgeon graduated with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">Bachelor of Laws</a> (Hons) in 1992 and a <a href="/wiki/Diploma_in_Legal_Practice" class="mw-redirect" title="Diploma in Legal Practice">Diploma in Legal Practice</a> the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> During her time at Glasgow University she was active as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_University_Scottish_Nationalist_Association" title="Glasgow University Scottish Nationalist Association">Glasgow University Scottish Nationalist Association</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Students%27_representative_council" title="Students&#39; representative council">students\' representative council</a>.\n</p><p>Following her graduation, Sturgeon completed her legal traineeship at McClure Naismith, a Glasgow firm of solicitors, in 1995. After qualifying as a <a href="/wiki/Solicitor" title="Solicitor">solicitor</a>, she worked for Bell &amp; Craig, a firm of solicitors in <a href="/wiki/Stirling" title="Stirling">Stirling</a>, and later at the <a href="/wiki/Drumchapel" title="Drumchapel">Drumchapel</a> <a href="/wiki/Law_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Law Centre">Law Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> from 1997 until her election to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_career">Early political career</span></h2>\n<p>Sturgeon joined the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP) in 1986, having already become a member of the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament" title="Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament">Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament</a>, and quickly became their Youth Affairs Vice Convener and Publicity Vice Convener.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She first stood for election in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1992" title="United Kingdom general election, 1992">1992 general election</a> as the SNP candidate in the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Shettleston_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Shettleston (UK Parliament constituency)">Glasgow Shettleston</a> constituency, and was the youngest parliamentary candidate in Scotland, failing to win the seat.\n</p><p>Sturgeon also stood unsuccessfully as the SNP candidate for the Irvine North <a href="/wiki/Ward_(electoral_subdivision)" title="Ward (electoral subdivision)">ward</a> on <a href="/wiki/Cunninghame" title="Cunninghame">Cunninghame</a> District Council in May 1992, for the <a href="/wiki/Baillieston" title="Baillieston">Baillieston</a>/<a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Glasgow" title="Mount Vernon, Glasgow">Mount Vernon</a> ward on <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde" title="Strathclyde">Strathclyde Regional Council</a> in 1994, and for the <a href="/wiki/Bridgeton,_Glasgow" title="Bridgeton, Glasgow">Bridgeton</a> ward on <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Council" title="Glasgow City Council">Glasgow City Council</a> in 1995.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In the mid-1990s, Sturgeon and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kennedy" title="Charles Kennedy">Charles Kennedy</a> went together on a political study visit to Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1997" title="United Kingdom general election, 1997">1997 general election</a> saw Sturgeon selected to fight the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Govan_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Govan (UK Parliament constituency)">Glasgow Govan</a> seat for the SNP. Boundary changes meant that the notional <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> majority in the seat had increased substantially. However, infighting between the two rival candidates for the Labour nomination, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Sarwar_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammad Sarwar (politician)">Mohammed Sarwar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Watson,_Baron_Watson_of_Invergowrie" title="Mike Watson, Baron Watson of Invergowrie">Mike Watson</a>, along with an energetic local campaign, resulted in Glasgow Govan being the only Scottish seat to see a swing away from Labour in the midst of a Labour <a href="/wiki/Landslide_victory" title="Landslide victory">landslide</a> nationwide. Sarwar did, however, win the seat with a majority of 2,914 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after this, Sturgeon was appointed as the SNP\'s spokesperson for energy and education matters.\n</p><p>Sturgeon stood for election to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliamentary_Election,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliamentary Election, 1999">first Scottish Parliament election</a> in 1999 as the SNP candidate for <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Govan_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Govan (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Glasgow Govan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Although she failed to win the seat, she was placed first in the SNP\'s regional list for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_(Scottish_Parliamentary_Electoral_Area)" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow (Scottish Parliamentary Electoral Area)">Glasgow region</a>, and was thus elected as a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Member of the Scottish Parliament</a>.  During the first term of the Scottish Parliament, Sturgeon served as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Shadow_Cabinet" title="Shadow Cabinet">Shadow Cabinets</a> of both <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Swinney" title="John Swinney">John Swinney</a>. She was <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Education_and_Lifelong_Learning" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Secretary for Education and Lifelong Learning">Shadow Minister for Children and Education</a> from 1999 to 2000, <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Health_and_Wellbeing" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing">Shadow Minister for Health and Community Care</a> from 2000 to 2003, and <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Justice" title="Cabinet Secretary for Justice">Shadow Minister for Justice</a> from 2003 to 2004. She also served as a member of the Education, Culture and Sport Committee and the Health and Community Care Committee.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Depute_Leader_and_Deputy_First_Minister">Depute Leader and Deputy First Minister</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Cabinet,_May_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg/220px-Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg/330px-Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg/440px-Scottish_Cabinet%2C_May_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="366" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Cabinet,_May_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon (front right) with Alex Salmond and the rest of the Scottish Government cabinet following election in 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>On 22 June 2004, John Swinney resigned as Leader of the SNP following poor results in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2004 (United Kingdom)">European Parliament election</a>. His then-depute, <a href="/wiki/Roseanna_Cunningham" title="Roseanna Cunningham">Roseanna Cunningham</a>, immediately announced her intention to stand for the leadership. The previous leader, Alex Salmond, announced at the time that he would not stand.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 24 June 2004, Sturgeon announced that she would also be a candidate in the forthcoming election for the leadership, with <a href="/wiki/Kenny_MacAskill" title="Kenny MacAskill">Kenny MacAskill</a> as her running mate.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, Salmond later announced that he did intend to stand for the leadership; Sturgeon subsequently withdrew from the contest and declared her support for Salmond, standing instead as his running mate for the depute leadership. It was reported that Salmond had privately supported Sturgeon in her leadership bid, but decided to run for the position himself as it became apparent she was unlikely to beat Cunningham.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The majority of the SNP hierarchy lent their support to the Salmond-Sturgeon bid for the leadership, although MSP <a href="/wiki/Alex_Neil_(politician)" title="Alex Neil (politician)">Alex Neil</a> backed Salmond as leader, but refused to endorse Sturgeon as depute.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The results of the leadership contest were announced on 3 September 2004, with Salmond and Sturgeon elected as Leader and Depute Leader respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> As Salmond was still an MP in the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a>, Sturgeon led the SNP at the Scottish Parliament until the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2007" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2007">2007 election</a>, when Salmond was elected as an MSP.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As leader of the SNP in the Scottish Parliament, Sturgeon became a high-profile figure in Scottish politics and often clashed with <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Jack_McConnell" title="Jack McConnell">Jack McConnell</a> at <a href="/wiki/First_Minister%27s_Question_Time_(Scotland)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Minister&#39;s Question Time (Scotland)">First Minister\'s Questions</a>. This included rows over the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons\'</a> decision to replace the Trident nuclear weapon system, and the SNP\'s plans to replace <a href="/wiki/Council_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Council tax">council tax</a> in Scotland with a <a href="/wiki/Local_income_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Local income tax">local income tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon defeated <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Jackson_(politician)" title="Gordon Jackson (politician)">Gordon Jackson</a> with a 4.7% swing to the SNP in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2007" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2007">2007 election</a> in Glasgow Govan. The election resulted in a hung parliament, with the SNP the largest party by a single seat; the SNP subsequently formed a minority government. Sturgeon was appointed as the <a href="/wiki/Deputy_First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="Deputy First Minister of Scotland">Deputy First Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Health_and_Wellbeing" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing">Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing</a> by <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister</a> Salmond. In the position she saw through party pledges such as scrapping prescription charges and reversing <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">accident and emergency</a> closures, she also became more widely known internationally for her handling of the <a href="/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic" title="2009 flu pandemic">2009 flu pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She was supported in her role as Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing by <a href="/wiki/Shona_Robison" title="Shona Robison">Shona Robison</a> MSP, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Public_Health_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Public Health and Sport">Minister for Public Health and Sport</a>, and by Alex Neil MSP, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Housing_and_Communities" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Housing and Communities">Minister for Housing and Communities</a>.\n</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2011" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2011">2011 election</a>, the SNP won a landslide victory and achieved a large overall majority. Sturgeon was retained as Deputy First Minister and Cabinet Secretary for Health and Wellbeing until a reshuffle one year later, when she was appointed as <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Infrastructure,_Investment_and_Cities" title="Cabinet Secretary for Infrastructure, Investment and Cities">Cabinet Secretary for Infrastructure, Investment and Cities</a> and an additional role overseeing the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">referendum on</a> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a>, essentially putting her in charge of the SNP\'s referendum campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, Sturgeon said that she believed that independence would allow Scotland to build a stronger and more competitive country, and would change spending priorities to address "the scandal of soaring poverty in a country as rich as Scotland".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 September 2014, independence was rejected in the Scottish independence referendum, with 55.3% of the voters voting no and 44.7% voting yes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a> campaign, Salmond announced his resignation as First Minister and Leader of the SNP. Sturgeon immediately announced that she would be a candidate in the election to replace him, and received huge support from the SNP hierarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon said that there would be "no greater privilege" than to lead the SNP. On Salmond\'s resignation, Sturgeon said:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>The personal debt of gratitude I owe Alex is immeasurable. He has been my friend, mentor and colleague for more than 20 years. Quite simply, I would not have been able to do what I have in politics without his constant advice, guidance and support through all these years. [...] I can think of no greater privilege than to seek to lead the party I joined when I was just 16. However, that decision is not for today.</p></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table,_June_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg/220px-Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg/330px-Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg/440px-Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table%2C_June_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3952" data-file-height="2504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Cabinet_around_the_Cabinet_Table,_June_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon (top right) seated with the 2007\xe2\x80\x932011 Scottish Cabinet following the SNP victory in the 2007 election</div></div></div>\n<p>Following the referendum defeat, Sturgeon said that "further devolution is the route to independence".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> She also opined that Scottish independence was a matter of "when, not if".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_the_Scottish_National_Party">Leadership of the Scottish National Party</span></h2>\n<p>On 24 September 2014, Sturgeon officially launched her campaign bid to succeed Salmond as Leader of the Scottish National Party at the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party_leadership_election,_2014" title="Scottish National Party leadership election, 2014">November leadership election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> It quickly became apparent that no other candidate would be able to receive enough required nominations to run a credible leadership campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> During the speech launching her campaign, Sturgeon announced that she would resign as Depute Leader, triggering a concurrent <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party_leadership_election,_2014" title="Scottish National Party leadership election, 2014">depute leadership election</a>; the MSPs <a href="/wiki/Angela_Constance" title="Angela Constance">Angela Constance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Brown_(Scottish_politician)" title="Keith Brown (Scottish politician)">Keith Brown</a> and the MP <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Hosie" title="Stewart Hosie">Stewart Hosie</a> all nominated themselves to succeed Sturgeon as Depute Leader.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nominations for the SNP leadership closed on 15 October, with Sturgeon confirmed as the only candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-SNP_leadership_elections_close_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNP_leadership_elections_close-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On this date, Sturgeon also came out on top in a trust rating opinion poll, conducted for the SNP, which indicated that 54% of the Scottish population trusted her to "stand up for Scotland\'s interests".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> After being confirmed as the only candidate, Sturgeon launched a tour of Scotland, visiting SNP members in different cities outlining her vision for Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon was formally acclaimed as the first female Leader of the SNP on 14 November 2014 at the Autumn Conference in <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Scotland" title="Perth, Scotland">Perth</a>, with Hosie as her depute. This also effectively made her First Minister in waiting, given the SNP\'s absolute majority in the Scottish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In her first speech as leader, Sturgeon said that it was "the privilege of her life" to lead the party she joined as a teenager.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Minister_of_Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="First_term.2C_2014.E2.80.932016"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_term,_2014\xe2\x80\x932016">First term, 2014\xe2\x80\x932016</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Minister,_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg/170px-First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg/255px-First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg/340px-First_Minister%2C_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="609" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Minister,_Nicola_Sturgeon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon\'s first term portrait as <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg/220px-Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg/330px-Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg/440px-Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3922" data-file-height="2801" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deputy_Secretary_Blinken_Meets_With_Scottish_First_Minister_Sturgeon_-_18490445358.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US Deputy Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Antony_Blinken" class="mw-redirect" title="Antony Blinken">Antony Blinken</a> meets with Nicola Sturgeon at the U.S. Department of State in Washington, D.C., on 10 June 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>On 19 November 2014, Salmond formally resigned as <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a> and the election for the new First Minister took place the following day. Sturgeon and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Davidson" title="Ruth Davidson">Ruth Davidson</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Conservative_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Conservative Party">Scottish Conservatives</a>, stood for election. Sturgeon received 66 votes, Davidson received 15 and there were 39 abstentions. As mentioned above, the SNP\'s absolute majority made Sturgeon\'s election all but certain.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon was formally sworn into office the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 20 November 2014, she was appointed to the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">Privy Council of the United Kingdom</a> and therefore granted the title, \'<a href="/wiki/The_Right_Honourable" title="The Right Honourable">The Right Honourable</a>\'.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 21 November, she unveiled her <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Cabinet">Cabinet</a> with a 50/50 gender balance, promoting <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Finance,_Employment_and_Sustainable_Growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Secretary for Finance, Employment and Sustainable Growth">Finance Secretary</a> John Swinney to become her <a href="/wiki/Deputy_First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="Deputy First Minister of Scotland">Deputy First Minister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By most accounts, Sturgeon took a more conciliatory approach to governing than Salmond.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  For instance, during her first First Minister\'s Questions after being sworn in, she said that she came into her new post "with an open mind and a willingness to hear proposals from all sides of the chamber."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_2015_general_election">UK 2015 general election</span></h4>\n<p>Sturgeon took part in several Scottish and UK-wide <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election_debates,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election debates, 2015">TV election debates</a> in the run up to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a> and according to opinion polls was regarded to have had a successful performance.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The SNP went on to win a <a href="/wiki/Landslide_victory" title="Landslide victory">landslide victory</a> in Scotland, winning 56 out of 59 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 April 2015, a leaked memo from the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland Office">Scotland Office</a> alleged that Sturgeon privately told the French ambassador <a href="/wiki/Sylvie_Bermann" title="Sylvie Bermann">Sylvie Bermann</a> that she would "rather see David Cameron remain as PM". This was in contrast to her publicly stated opposition to a Conservative Government on the run up to the election.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The memo was quickly denied by both Sturgeon and the French consulate.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> It was later noted that the memo had contained a disclaimer that parts of the conversation may have been "lost in translation" and its release had been ordered by then <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Scotland" title="Secretary of State for Scotland">Scottish Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Carmichael" title="Alistair Carmichael">Alistair Carmichael</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon stated that Carmichael had "engaged in dirty tricks" and that he should consider his position as an <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Scottish_Parliament_election.2C_2016"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_Parliament_election,_2016">Scottish Parliament election, 2016</span></h4>\n<p>Sturgeon contested her first election as SNP leader at the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2016" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2016">2016 election</a>. The SNP fell two seats short of securing another overall majority. Nonetheless, with 63 seats, the SNP was still by far the largest party in the chamber, with more than double the seats of the next-largest party, the Scottish Tories.<sup id="cite_ref-results_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-results-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-map_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon was formally nominated for a second term on 17 May, defeating Lib Dem leader <a href="/wiki/Willie_Rennie" title="Willie Rennie">Willie Rennie</a> by a vote of 63 to 5, with 59 members abstaining.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Second_term.2C_2016.E2.80.93"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_term,_2016\xe2\x80\x93">Second term, 2016\xe2\x80\x93</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_EU_membership_referendum">2016 EU membership referendum</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg/220px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg/330px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg/440px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="388" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_EU_diplomats_following_the_Brexit_result.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets diplomats from 27 <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> countries at <a href="/wiki/Bute_House" title="Bute House">Bute House</a> to address the rights and conditions of EU nationals resident in Scotland following the EU referendum result</div></div></div>\n<p>The UK Government held a referendum to decide the future of the United Kingdom\'s European Union membership in which all 32 council areas in Scotland voted by a majority for the United Kingdom to remain a member of the EU. Across Scotland, 62% of voters backed the UK remaining a member of the EU, with 38% voting for the UK to leave. Overall 52% of voters in the United Kingdom voted to leave the EU, with 48% voting to remain.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In response to the result, on 24 June 2016, Sturgeon said that <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> officials would begin planning for a second independence referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon claimed that it was "clear that the people of Scotland see their future as part of the European Union" and that Scotland had "spoken decisively" with a "strong, unequivocal" vote to remain in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-ft2_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon said it was "democratically unacceptable" that Scotland could be taken out of the EU "against its will".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 June, Sturgeon said she would communicate to all EU member states that Scotland had voted to stay in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> An emergency Scottish cabinet meeting on 25 June agreed that the Scottish Government would seek to enter negotiations with the EU and its member states, to explore options to protect Scotland\xe2\x80\x99s place in the EU."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stv250616_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stv250616-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon later said that while she believed in Scottish independence, her starting point in these discussions was to protect Scotland\'s relationship with the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> May\'s comments confirmed that the PM wanted the Scottish government to be "fully engaged" in the process.\n</p><p>Sturgeon was planning to meet with EU leaders in Brussels to discuss Scotland remaining in the EU. However, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a>, President of the European Council, said that such discussions would be "not appropriate" considering the "situation in the UK".<sup id="cite_ref-johnson1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson1-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, she was able to arrange for a meeting on 29 June with European Parliament President <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, Sturgeon said the reception had been "sympathetic", but she conceded that she did not underestimate the challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg/250px-First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg" width="250" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg/375px-First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg/500px-First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="441" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Minister_meets_the_Prime_Minister_at_Bute_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon welcomes British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bute_House" title="Bute House">Bute House</a>, 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>Sturgeon met with new UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> in Edinburgh on 15 July 2016 after the latter had made it clear that UK unity was a high priority.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, Sturgeon said that "It would be inconceivable for any prime minister to seek to stand in the way of a referendum if that is what the Scottish Parliament voted for ... if there\'s a clear sense that that\'s what people in Scotland want, would be completely the wrong thing to do." She added a conciliatory note, however in her assessment of May: "She\'s a woman who has a fairly businesslike way of doing things, which I have too. So I think we can find a way of working together, notwithstanding those disagreements."<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_referendum_on_independence">Future referendum on independence</span></h4>\n<p>Sturgeon confirmed in June 2016 that the Scottish government has formally agreed to draft legislation to allow a second independence referendum to take place.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> As the constitution is a \'reserved\' matter under the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>, for a future referendum on Scottish independence to be binding under UK law, it would need to receive the consent of the British Parliament to take place.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 June 2016 Sturgeon made it clear that her motion to begin discussions with the EU (for Scotland to remain in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>) did not constitute a proposal for a second referendum on independence.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> However, her statements indicated that she had parliamentary authority to explore "options" for keeping Scotland in the EU, "including independence".<sup id="cite_ref-johnson1_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson1-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> By 13 October 2016, she announced the first formal step towards launching a new referendum, called the "Independence Referendum Bill".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc13octobersnpsnicolasturgeonannounces_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc13octobersnpsnicolasturgeonannounces-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prior to the day the Prime Minister triggered <a href="/wiki/Article_50" class="mw-redirect" title="Article 50">Article 50</a>, formally allowing the process of the United Kingdom leaving the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> voted 69 to 59 in favour of another independence referendum,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> formally giving Sturgeon the legal mandate to write to Theresa May to allow another referendum to take place. By the end of that week, on 30 March 2017, Sturgeon wrote to the Prime Minister requesting a Section 30 order, formally devolving the responsibility and power to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> to plan for and hold another referendum on Scottish Independence.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Previously, May and <a href="/wiki/David_Mundell" title="David Mundell">David Mundell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Scotland" title="Secretary of State for Scotland">Secretary of State for Scotland</a>, have both highlighted that as the negotiations begin with the European Union on the United Kingdom\'s withdraw, it is important for Scotland to work with the UK Government to get the best exit deal for both the United Kingdom and Scotland, stating that "now is not the time for another referendum".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union_membership">European Union membership</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg/220px-FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg/330px-FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg/440px-FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FM_meets_with_Juncker.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets with <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> in 2016 to discuss Brexit</div></div></div>\n<p>Following the 2016 UK referendum on the exiting the European Union, Sturgeon has called for Scotland\'s place in the European single market to be protected.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In response to the UK-wide vote for the United Kingdom to leave the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>, headed by Sturgeon, launched the <i>Scotland\'s Place in Europe</i> document, a white paper setting out the Scottish Government\'s aims and wishes of Scotland\'s role in Europe post-Brexit. The paper was sent to the central <a href="/wiki/British_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="British Government">British Government</a> to be read by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>. <i>Scotland\'s Place in Europe</i> was the first post-Brexit strategy by any government in the British isles, including the central UK Government who pushed ahead to hold the vote in June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The document, published in December 2016, seeks for Scotland to remain a member of the European Single Market to allow the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Scotland" title="Economy of Scotland">Economy of Scotland</a> to benefit from free trade deals across the remaining 27 European Union nations. Furthermore, it seeks that remaining within the European Single Market would be beneficial for trade across the entire United Kingdom, whereby it benefits the economies of both Scotland and the United Kingdom as well as benefiting the wider economy and trade of the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Within <i>Scotland\'s Place in Europe</i>, the Scottish Government highlights that there are several ways that Scotland could retain its membership of the European Single Market, but most notably by becoming an independent sovereign country within the EU which is the preferred option of Sturgeon and the wider SNP led-Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Other than trade and single market membership, Sturgeon advocates the importance of the rights of EU nationals currently working and residing within Scotland and that there rights and liberties are protected post-Brexit.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As immigration and border controls remain a reserved matter,<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.scot_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament.scot-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon has called on strong working with Prime Minister Theresa May and the UK Government to ensure this is achieved. Other issues set in the document include protection over laws and legislation which affects Scotland, protection of worker\'s rights and entitlements, a review of the devolution settlement in Scotland that will be affected by Brexit such as farming and fishery industries and additional powers granted to Scotland to protect and promote Scottish interests.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recently, Sturgeon has advocated for a second independence referendum to be held at the end of the Brexit process which is expected around 2019, claiming that there is "too much at stake for Scotland for the Brexit process to be imposed<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>". A week prior to the Brexit negotiations beginning between the UK Government, 27 EU member state governments and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, Sturgeon called on Prime Minister Theresa May to "pause" Brexit negotiations to allow for the creation of a four way government approach to Brexit involving the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Government" title="Welsh Government">Welsh Government</a>, UK Government and Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, Sturgeon criticised the approaches taken by both Theresa May and the British Government towards the Brexit approach, claiming that May "will struggle" as she is a "difficult person to build a rapport with". In the same interview, Sturgeon committed to no independence referendum being held prior to the terms of a UK wide Brexit deal being agreed and presented.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with First Minister of Wales Carwyn Jones, Sturgeon criticised in a statement the Brexit repeal bill to convert EU law into British law as a "power grab", because the bill "does not return powers from the EU to the devolved administrations, as promised" but "returns them solely to the UK government and parliament, and imposes new restrictions on the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> These fears were reiterated in September, when the Scottsh devolved government recommened its Parliament to withhold its consent for the bill. Scotland and Wales are expected to propose amendments to the bill.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With a view towards Brexit, Sturgeon demanded greater powers for the Scottish Parliament, arguing that Brexit is threatening Scotland\'s <a href="/wiki/Scottish_devolution_settlement" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish devolution settlement">devolution settlement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> With London seeking to restrict immigration to the United Kingdom, she asserted that Scotland should be able to set its own immigration policy, as well as policies relating to employment and trade.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Scottish_local_elections.2C_2017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_local_elections,_2017">Scottish local elections, 2017</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_local_elections,_2017" title="Scottish local elections, 2017">Scottish local elections, 2017</a></div>\n<p>Sturgeon and the SNP went into the Scottish council elections that were held on 4 May 2017, as the largest political party in the 32 local council areas in Scotland, having 424 councillors elected to serve on the councils across Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Opinion polling for the council elections conducted in early 2017 suggested that the SNP looked set to repeat this level of success, with 47% of the public claiming they will be voting for SNP candidates on election day.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  Publicly speaking about the 2017 Scottish council elections, Sturgeon has said that the elections were a clear choice between voting for herself and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Davidson" title="Ruth Davidson">Ruth Davidson</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Conservative_and_Unionist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Conservative and Unionist Party">Scottish Conservative and Unionist Party</a>, citing the stark fall in support of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Labour_Party" title="Scottish Labour Party">Scottish Labour Party</a> and their leader <a href="/wiki/Kezia_Dugdale" title="Kezia Dugdale">Kezia Dugdale</a> over the past several years.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Whilst failing to win any outright overall control in any council area in Scotland, the SNP emerged as the largest political group in sixteen councils, including <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Council" title="Glasgow City Council">Glasgow City Council</a>, knocking the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Labour_Party" title="Scottish Labour Party">Scottish Labour Party</a> out of power in Glasgow for the first time since 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The SNP increased their number of councillors elected in 2017 than it did in 2012, with 431 being elected, compared to 425 in the 2012 local elections.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The SNP became the largest political party in council areas such as <a href="/wiki/Falkirk_(council_area)" class="mw-redirect" title="Falkirk (council area)">Falkirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Edinburgh_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Edinburgh Council">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_City_Council" title="Aberdeen City Council">Aberdeen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Following the results, Sturgeon claimed that the election was a "clear and emphatic victory for the SNP\', despite the large number of seats gained by the Scottish Conservatives.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg/220px-Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg/330px-Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg/440px-Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sturgeon_visits_Hong_Kong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets with <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Lam" title="Carrie Lam">Carrie Lam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_of_Hong_Kong" title="Chief Executive of Hong Kong">Chief Executive of Hong Kong</a> during a trade visit, 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>Whilst foreign policy remains a reserved matter,<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.scot_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament.scot-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> the Scottish Government still has the power and ability to strengthen and develop Scotland, the economy and Scottish interests on the world stage and encourage foreign businesses, international devolved, regional and central governments to invest in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon has undertaken a number of visits to Europe, North America and Asia to promote Scotland as a place of investment and Scottish businesses and partners to trade and do business with.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon has committed to strengthening links between Scotland and the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> continent, stating that Scotland has a long-standing reputation on the world stage as being a key partner with African countries where it has funded and developed a number of projects.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since becoming First Minister in 2014, Sturgeon has visited the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (and states including <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>). During the 2017 visit to the United States, Sturgeon met with <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor of California</a> where both Brown and Sturgeon signed an agreement which commits both the Government of California and Scottish Government to work together to tackle climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Other engagements included meeting CEO of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> <a href="/wiki/Tim_Cook" title="Tim Cook">Tim Cook</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and signing a \xc2\xa36.3 million deal for Scottish investment from American businesses and firms which promotes aspects of Scotland such as trade, tourism and innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon has sought to continue the strong connections and bond between Scotland and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. During an official visit to the Republic of Ireland in 2016, speaking in Dublin, Sturgeon claimed that is it "important for Ireland and Scotland and the whole of the British Isles that Ireland has a strong ally in Scotland".<sup id="cite_ref-firstminister.gov.scot_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstminister.gov.scot-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> During the same engagement, Sturgeon became the first head of government to address the <a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the Upper House of the Irish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-firstminister.gov.scot_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstminister.gov.scot-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon used her speech to the house to highlights the troubles ahead for both the Irish and Scottish Governments posed by the Brexit vote, but vowed to "bring benefits" to the British Isles and to "make new work" for both Ireland and Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-firstminister.gov.scot_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstminister.gov.scot-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg/220px-FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg/330px-FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg/440px-FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="528" data-file-height="409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FM_Meets_German_Minister_of_Europe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets with <a href="/wiki/German_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="German Government">German Government</a> <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_for_Europe" title="Minister of State for Europe">Minister of State for Europe</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Roth_(politician)" title="Michael Roth (politician)">Michael Roth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, August 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>In August 2016, Sturgeon travelled to <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to meet with the <a href="/wiki/German_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="German Government">German Government</a> to discuss the results of the European Union referendum in which the United Kingdom voted to leave as well as discussing the next steps open to the European Union, the United Kingdom and Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon met with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Roth_(politician)" title="Michael Roth (politician)">Michael Roth</a>, Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_for_Europe" title="Minister of State for Europe">Minister of State for Europe</a> during the visit, highlighting to the German Government that Scotland as a whole voted to remain within the European Union despite the nationwide UK vote being to leave", with Roth highlighting that the talks were "very productive" and hoped that the "UK would find a way" that will benefit Europe and Scotland in the end.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In response to the Brexit vote and with the intention to protect Scotland\'s interests and democratic vote to remain within the European Union, Sturgeon has travelled to <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> to meet with both <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a>. At the engagement in June 2016, Sturgeon highlighted the concerns raised in Scotland by the Brexit vote and claimed that Scotland\'s desire to remain within the European Union was met with "sympathy" from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon spoke at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> about gender equality and human rights, claiming that she is "determined" to use her powers as First Minister of Scotland to "make things better" and "improve opportunities" for women. Sturgeon also highlighted that Scotland is determined to "play our part in co-operation with others, to help to achieve peace and security".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Catalonian_independence_referendum.2C_2017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Catalonian_independence_referendum,_2017">Catalonian independence referendum, 2017</span></h4>\n<p>In the run up to the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_referendum,_2017" title="Catalan independence referendum, 2017">Catalan independence referendum, 2017</a>, Nicola Sturgeon offered her own personal backing and that of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> to <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> in the holding of a democratic and fair independence referendum, stating that "self determination was an important principle".<sup id="cite_ref-Archived_copy_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archived_copy-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Government of Spain has criticised Sturgeon for her comments and intervention to the independence movement in Catalonia, claiming that Sturgeon had "totally misunderstood" the situation in Spain and Catalonia.<sup id="cite_ref-Archived_copy_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archived_copy-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In response to the mass police attacks and violence against Catalans on polling day, Sturgeon expressed her personal concern over the situation in Catalonia and the response shown by the Spanish Government and the Spanish police, claiming that all should condemn the violence taking place "regardless of their views on independence" and that the central Spanish Government in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> should allow the polling to take place before "someone gets hurt" as a result of violence.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations,_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg/220px-Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg/330px-Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg/440px-Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations%2C_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sturgeon_addresses_the_United_Nations,_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon delivering a speech at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in New York City</div></div></div>\n<p>In the run up to the Scottish independence referendum in 2014, then <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> offered his support to the <a href="/wiki/Better_Together_(campaign)" title="Better Together (campaign)">Better Together</a> side, claiming that the United Kingdom was better united, with Scotland remaining within it. There was much speculation that Obama\'s last minute intervention in the referendum debate and offering his support to a "strong, robust and united" United Kingdom was due to concerns in <a href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Washington D.C.">Washington D.C.</a> that one of the United States\' closest allies could separate and weaken the relation between the United States and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon was highly critical of Obama\'s intervention in the debate, claiming that his intervention "helped" boost the number of votes <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a> received. Sturgeon claimed she was not "sore" about the intervention shown by Barack Obama, but his claim about a strong United Kingdom had a "strange" impact on Scots.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon was highly critical of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> during the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">United States presidential election, 2016</a> and had publicly backed his <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> rival <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon had been highly critical of Donald Trump and his policies, highlighting her disapproval of his language and views relating to sexism and misogyny, and stating upon Trump\'s victory that she hopes "Trump turns out to be a president different to the one he was during his campaign and reaches out to those who felt vilified by his campaign".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Upon Trump\'s victory during the Presidential election, Sturgeon and Trump spoke on the phone to discuss the future relationship and diplomatic approaches between both the United States and Scotland with Sturgeon offering her well wishes to Trump following his success. Sturgeon highlighted that "Scotland and the United States will continue to cooperate in those areas where we share common interests and goals, and when appropriate we will also look to have constructive dialogue on issues where our views differ".<sup id="cite_ref-stv.tv_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stv.tv-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon had also previously stripped Donald Trump of his ambassadorial role for Scottish businesses with the Scottish Government in the aftermath of Trump\'s views of an outright ban of <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> from entering the United States. Sturgeon claimed following comments made by Trump in relation to Muslims entering the United States that he was "not fit" for the ambassadorial role with the Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-stv.tv_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stv.tv-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and its former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a> had always been highly critical and against the idea of an independent Scotland, with Rajoy always claiming that Scotland would be "outside" of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> should it have voted for independence from the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Whilst the Scottish Government and Sturgeon had argued that due to being a current member of the European Union as part of the United Kingdom that Scotland would be granted automatic entry as it jointed the European Union as part of the United Kingdom in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> However, Spain had always doubted that theory and viewpoint of the Scottish Government, claiming that Scotland would be waiting a number of years to gain entry to the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the aftermath of the United Kingdom\'s decision to withdraw its membership of the European Union, Prime Minister Rajoy once again was critical of the views taken by the Scottish Government when he rejected calls from Sturgeon for Scotland to remain within the European Single Market.
