The Spanish Secretary of State to the European Union, Jorge Toledo, claimed that "if the United Kingdom leaves the single market then the whole United Kingdom leaves the single market" going onto claim further that there is only "one negotiator that is the UK Government<sup id="cite_ref-holyrood.com_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holyrood.com-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>". Mariano Rajoy told the meeting of the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> that he was block any independent and separate deal put forward by Sturgeon and the Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-holyrood.com_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holyrood.com-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan,_German_Minister,_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg/220px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg/330px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg/440px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan%2C_German_Minister%2C_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2117" data-file-height="2167" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Niels_Annan,_German_Minister,_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets with <a href="/wiki/Niels_Annen" title="Niels Annen">Niels Annen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State" title="Minister of State">Minister of State</a> at the German <a href="/wiki/Federal_Foreign_Office" title="Federal Foreign Office">Federal Foreign Office</a>, June 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>Sturgeon has been highly critical of the Spanish Governments actions and the way it has dealt with the affairs relating to the Catalan independence referendum held in October 2017, highlighting to Mariano Rajoy that instead he should follow "the shining example" that was created as part of the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Agreement_(2012)" title="Edinburgh Agreement (2012)">Edinburgh Agreement</a> between the Scottish and British Governments that allowed Scotland to hold a legally binding referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span></h4>\n<p>In 2016, it was announced by Sturgeon that she would be opening a Scottish embassy in Germany to strengthen international relations between both <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In June 2018, Sturgeon travelled to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> with representatives from twelve Scottish based companies on a trade delegation to promote inwards investment in Scotland and to promote and strengthen trading connections with Germany. Sturgeon also met with <a href="/wiki/Niels_Annen" title="Niels Annen">Niels Annen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State" title="Minister of State">Minister of State</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Foreign_Office" title="Federal Foreign Office">Federal Foreign Office</a>, marking the first meeting between the Scottish Government and the new German Government which was elected under the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Merkel_cabinet" title="Fourth Merkel cabinet">Fourth Merkel cabinet</a> in March 2018. Furthermore, Sturgeon met with <a href="/wiki/Michael_M%C3%BCller_(politician)" title="Michael M\xc3\xbcller (politician)">Michael M\xc3\xbcller</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Governing_Mayor_of_Berlin" title="Governing Mayor of Berlin">Governing Mayor of Berlin</a> to discuss the future cooperation around the <a href="/wiki/2018_European_Championships" title="2018 European Championships">2018 European Championships</a>, being held in Glasgow and Berlin in August.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Ireland">Republic of Ireland</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins,_President_of_Ireland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg/220px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg/330px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg/440px-Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins%2C_President_of_Ireland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="485" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicola_Sturgeon_meets_with_Michael_Higgins,_President_of_Ireland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sturgeon meets Irish President <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As First Minister, Sturgeon has endured a long-standing relationship with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Government of Ireland</a>, meeting regularly with both <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a> and his successor, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a>. Sturgeon claims that the relationship between Scotland and the Republic of Ireland is "more important than ever", with Sturgeon completing numerous trips to the Republic of Ireland to continue to promote Scottish trade and business, cultural and economic ties between the Republic of Ireland and Scotland, as well as strengthening Irish-Scottish relations.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> As part of the <a href="/wiki/British-Irish_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="British-Irish Council">British-Irish Council</a>, members of both the Scottish Government and Government of Ireland meet regularly to discuss and agree on areas of mutual concern and interest relating to the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Sturgeon was invited to address the <a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the upper house of the Parliament of the Republic of Ireland, making her the first serving head of government in the world to address the Seanad \xc3\x89ireann.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceD_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon used her speech of the parliament to highlight the "long tradition of co-operation" between Scotland and the Republic of Ireland, stating that this was "even more important" since the British vote to withdraw from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceD_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> During the same visit, Sturgeon met <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President of Ireland</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Charles_Flanagan" title="Charles Flanagan">Charles Flanagan</a>, the minister for foreign affairs, during her visit to <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the decision to leave the European Union, Sturgeon has endured a strong relationship with the Republic of Ireland to ensure a strong Scottish deal and to explore options relating to trade can continue once the United Kingdom leaves the European Union. In June 2018, Sturgeon, Varadkar and <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Wales" title="First Minister of Wales">First Minister of Wales</a> <a href="/wiki/Carwyn_Jones" title="Carwyn Jones">Carwyn Jones</a> held an emergency summit in the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> where Varadkar highlighted that the Republic of Ireland was preparing for a "no deal Brexit". In response, both Sturgeon and Jones issued a joint ministerial statement to put pressure on Prime Minister Theresa May to reconsider her stance on withdrawing the United Kingdom from the EU Customs Union.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views">Political views</span></h2>\n<p>Sturgeon has campaigned against replacing the <a href="/wiki/Trident_nuclear_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="Trident nuclear programme">Trident nuclear weapons system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> She has been a critic of austerity, saying that the UK government\'s "austerity economics" is "morally unjustifiable and economically unsustainable".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sturgeon is noted for campaigning for <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women&#39;s rights">women\'s rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, and is a self-described <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminist</a>; she has argued that Scotland\'s feminist movement is not simply symbolic, but "sends a powerful signal about equality".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> She has hailed Scottish feminist economist <a href="/wiki/Ailsa_McKay" title="Ailsa McKay">Ailsa McKay</a> as one of her inspirations.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_acknowledgements">Awards and acknowledgements</span></h2>\n<p>Sturgeon won the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Politician_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Politician of the Year Award">Scottish Politician of the Year Award</a> in 2008, 2012 and 2014. In 2004, 2008 and 2011 she also won the <i><a href="/wiki/Donald_Dewar" title="Donald Dewar">Donald Dewar</a> Debater of the Year Award</i> at the same event, which is organized by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Herald_(Glasgow)" title="The Herald (Glasgow)">The Herald</a></i> newspaper.\n</p><p>In February 2013, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Hour" title="Woman&#39;s Hour">Woman\'s Hour</a></i> assessed Sturgeon as being the 20th most powerful woman in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> She rose to be listed as the most powerful and influential in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<p>Sturgeon lives in Glasgow with her husband, Peter Murrell, who is the current chief executive of the SNP.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The couple have been in a relationship since 2003. They announced their engagement on 29 January 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and were married on 16 July 2010 at \xc3\x92ran M\xc3\xb3r in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Her mother Joan was the SNP Provost of <a href="/wiki/North_Ayrshire" title="North Ayrshire">North Ayrshire</a> council, where she was councillor for the Irvine East ward since 2007 until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Sturgeon does not have children. In 2016 she disclosed that she had a miscarriage in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Hour" title="Woman&#39;s Hour">BBC\'s Women\'s Hour</a>, Sturgeon revealed that it was <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> that inspired her to enter politics, because, due to rising unemployment in Scotland at the time, she developed "a strong feeling that it was wrong for Scotland to be governed by a Tory government that we hadn\'t elected".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_First_Ministers_of_Scotland" title="List of First Ministers of Scotland">List of First Ministers of Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_current_heads_of_government_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_dependencies" title="List of current heads of government in the United Kingdom and dependencies">List of current heads of government in the United Kingdom and dependencies</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
